## Analysis

The Ground Truth (GT) expression is:
`-0.826056547542989*v - 2.45151654379511*x**3 - 0.413028273771494*log(Abs(v) + 1) + 0.340325443007139*sin(t)`

The key components are:
1. A term linear in `v`: `-0.826*v`
2. A term `x**3`: `-2.45*x**3`
3. A **logarithmic term** in `v`: `-0.413*log(|v| + 1)`
4. A sinusoidal term: `0.34*sin(t)`

The critical feature is the `log(|v| + 1)` term. This is a logarithmic function of `v` that cannot be represented by:
- Polynomial terms in `v` (like `v`, `v**2`, `v**3`, `v*|v|`)
- Exponential terms in `x`
- Sinusoidal terms
- Rational terms

Let me check each candidate for the ability to produce a `log(|v| + 1)` term:

**None of the candidates contain a `log()` function applied to `v`.** The candidates use combinations of:
- Polynomial terms in `x` and `v` (including `v*|v|`, `v**3`, `v*x`, etc.)
- Exponential functions of `x` or `sin(t)`
- Trigonometric functions of `t` and `x`
- Rational functions of `x`

Candidate 25 has `log(c8*exp(c9*x) + 1)` but this is a function of `x` only, not `v`.

The `log(|v| + 1)` term is fundamentally nonlinear in `v` in a way that cannot be captured by any finite polynomial in `v`, nor by `v*|v|`, `v**3`, or any other term present in the candidates. While some candidates might approximate the GT well numerically over a limited range, none can be made **exactly equivalent** for all values of `v`.

No candidate can reproduce the logarithmic dependence on `v`, so no match exists.

Conclusion: No match

**GT:** `-0.826056547542989*v - 2.45151654379511*x**3 - 0.413028273771494*log(Abs(v) + 1) + 0.340325443007139*sin(t)`

The GT has these basis functions:
1. `v` (linear in v)
2. `x**3` (cubic in x)
3. `log(Abs(v) + 1)` (logarithmic in |v|)
4. `sin(t)` (sinusoidal in t)

Key observations:
- The GT contains `log(Abs(v) + 1)`, which is a very specific nonlinear function of v
- No `x**2`, no `x`, no constant term, no `v*x`, no `v*Abs(v)`, no `exp(...)` terms
- The sin term is purely `sin(t)` with no phase shift needed (or phase can be absorbed)

Let me check each candidate for whether it can produce the `log(Abs(v) + 1)` term. Since none of the candidates contain a `log` function explicitly, I need to check if any combination of their terms can reproduce it.

**Critical insight:** The GT has `log(Abs(v) + 1)` which is NOT equivalent to any polynomial in v, `v*Abs(v)`, `v**3`, `exp(...)`, or any other basis function present in the candidates. Since `log(Abs(v) + 1)` is linearly independent from all polynomial, exponential, trigonometric, and `v*Abs(v)` type functions, NO candidate can match unless it contains a `log` term involving `v`.

Let me scan all 50 candidates for any `log` term involving `v`:
- Candidate 25: has `log(c8*exp(c9*x) + 1)` — this is a function of x, not v
- Candidate 36: has `exp(c7*v)` — exponential in v, not log
- No other candidate has `log` at all

None of the candidates contain `log(Abs(v) + ...)` or any equivalent.

Since `log(Abs(v) + 1)` is linearly independent from all basis functions present in any candidate (polynomials in v, `v*Abs(v)`, `v**3`, exponentials, trigonometric functions, etc.), no candidate can exactly match the GT.

Let me verify this is not approximable by `v*Abs(v)` or similar: `log(Abs(v)+1)` behaves like `|v|` for small v and like `log|v|` for large v, while `v*Abs(v) = |v|*v` grows quadratically. These are fundamentally different functions — not equivalent.
